<div id="review_185975949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185975949" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/298806-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452743476p2/298806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185975949?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/298806-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312614799" href="/book/show/10368915-soul-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298806-rachel?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185975949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13552200454176504263">Things in Atlanta are a mess. The Guild can’t get a handle on their local demon population and it looks like the Hunters from Rome will have to step in and help. But their kind of help always comes at a price.<br/><br/>No one is sure what happened at the Guild meeting that landed several trappers in the morgue and others severely injured. But whatever it was, someone is to blame and it looks like everyone wants to point the finger at Riley and Paul Blackthorne.<br/><br/>On top of all of this, Riley is still trying </span>
  <span id="freeText13552200454176504263" style="display:none">Things in Atlanta are a mess. The Guild can’t get a handle on their local demon population and it looks like the Hunters from Rome will have to step in and help. But their kind of help always comes at a price.<br /><br />No one is sure what happened at the Guild meeting that landed several trappers in the morgue and others severely injured. But whatever it was, someone is to blame and it looks like everyone wants to point the finger at Riley and Paul Blackthorne.<br /><br />On top of all of this, Riley is still trying to figure out why she’s being specifically targeted by a Grade Five Geo-Fiend and who could have wanted her father so badly yet hasn’t come forward to brag about their success. Plus, her love life has taken a serious turn for the worse. And she was so sure she’d found the perfect boyfriend.<br /><br />With Denver Beck practically ignoring her except when he’s telling her what to do and Simon still trying to come to terms with what happened to him, Riley only has one shoulder to lean on and that’s Ori’s – a freelance Hunter who has assigned himself as her personal bodyguard.<br /><br />Having someone who is tall, dark and dangerous looking out for her can’t be all bad. And no matter what Beck says, she’s not about to stay away from Ori. Besides, if Beck can play with danger, in the form of a red-headed reporter, why can’t she?<br /><br />***<br /><br />Soul Thief is yet another fast-paced, exciting and gripping young adult novel from author Jana Oliver. The action picks up right where it left off at the end of the first book, The Demon Trapper’s Daughter. Atlanta is in chaos. The trappers are shell-shocked and still trying to regroup after the attack at the Tabernacle.<br /><br />Riley is desperately trying to get answers about who’s behind what happened to her father, Beck is enlisted as one of the spokespersons for the Guild now that they’ve caught the attention of the Vatican, and the demon who has been after her is still out there somewhere, biding his time.<br /><br />Jana Oliver has written a sequel that not only continues the events from the first book, but builds on them. She expands her world and gives her characters even more dimension.<br /><br />Her main character, Riley Blackthorne, is still tough, reckless, brave and stubborn, but the author also shows a side of her that is sympathetic, fragile and incredibly lovable. And she gives readers greater insight into Denver Beck’s thoughts and emotions. She shows a softer side of Beck, while not taking away from any of his strength. He is still fiercely protective of Riley, loyal to Paul, and a trapper through and through.<br /><br />While the trapping of demons has been moved to the background in this book, there are several new threats to Riley and the Atlanta Trappers. The Demon Hunters of Rome, the Priest that oversees them, and the powerful force behind what happened to Paul Blackthorne are the new and dangerous, perhaps even deadly, ingredients added to the mix.<br /><br />Many questions are answered, but even more are raised, and a surprise twist takes this in a new direction and leaves events at a cliffhanger at the story’s end.<br /><br />Soul Thief is undoubtedly a must read, not only for fans of the first book, but for readers who love their main characters with a bit of an edge, demons who are not smokin’ hot, just smoking, and a plot that will keep them glued to the pages right from the start. It is action-packed, tension-filled and one heck of a great read.<br /><br />(This one got my 6 star rating on the blog.)<br /><br />On a personal note:<br /><br />This book so blew The Demon Trapper’s Daughter out of the water. And I freaking loved that book. But this book…I can’t even begin to tell you just how much this one slaughtered me.<br /><br />I became obsessed with this series when I received an early copy of The Demon Trapper’s Daughter last year from a Goodreads win. It had a completely different feel to any other story about demons that I had read up to that point. There were no hot demon boys – those demons were really disgusting, some of whom were seriously vicious. But there were definitely a few hotties – hello, Den Beck. And in Soul Thief Ori is definitely some major competition.<br /><br />I read this book in one fairly long sitting. I did take my time with it as I saw absolutely no reason to rush and possibly miss something key. And besides, the longer I took to read it, the more time I could spend with Den, Ori and Riley.<br /><br />Riley and Den absolutely tortured me in good and bad ways. They are just so perfect for each other – they are both trappers and both are incredibly stubborn and fiercely protective.<br /><br />I practically can’t talk about anything because there are just so many ways to unintentionally reveal spoilers, especially about Ori and Simon, who play major parts in the book. But I will say that there was a lot more of a mystery in Soul Thief as the characters tried to figure out what was behind what happened at the Guild meeting at the end of the last book.<br /><br />I love the way Jana Oliver makes her readers think they know everything when the characters don’t, but in actuality she’s only giving us a peek at what’s going on. Misleading us into believing one thing, when whammo it is something so totally else.<br /><br />There were a few definite foreshadow moments that got me to thinking, which I might have missed if I had read it any quicker. So the ending didn’t completely come out of left field. But I did not expect everything that happened. Oh Riley, what did you do?<br /><br />I loved Den Beck way more in Soul Thief. I really didn’t think that was possible, but so much more was revealed about him that made him that even more swoon-worthy – he allowed some of his feelings and his vulnerability to show.<br /><br />The U.S. title is absolutely perfect for the book as, just like the first book, it means something to the story and is not just some arbitrary title.<br /><br />I am dying to read the next book and I will be cruelly suffering until it’s released, because that ending leaves so much up in the air. So many ways for things to get even worse. So many possibilities for a really, really bad outcome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13552200454176504263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_310959674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310959674" />
    <a title="Shelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley"><img alt="Shelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420295300p2/3081722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310959674?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelley" href="/user/show/3081722-shelley">Shelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312614799" href="/book/show/10368915-soul-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=2011-releases">2011-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081722-shelley?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310959674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16995320266099880533">Genre: YA Paranormal<br/>Rating: 3.5-4 stars<br/><br/>*Review*<br/><br/>17-year old apprentice demon trapper Riley Blackthorne's world is about to abruptly change and dive rapidly into the abyss thanks to several factors that are all working against her. Most of these factors have absolutely nothing whatsoever to do with Riley or her actions which are intended to be brave in nature, but silly once they are made.<br/><br/>Her father's body has been raised from the dead by an unknown force and nobody is talking about it. The necrom</span>
  <span id="freeText16995320266099880533" style="display:none">Genre: YA Paranormal<br />Rating: 3.5-4 stars<br /><br />*Review*<br /><br />17-year old apprentice demon trapper Riley Blackthorne's world is about to abruptly change and dive rapidly into the abyss thanks to several factors that are all working against her. Most of these factors have absolutely nothing whatsoever to do with Riley or her actions which are intended to be brave in nature, but silly once they are made.<br /><br />Her father's body has been raised from the dead by an unknown force and nobody is talking about it. The necromancers that Riley knew from protecting her fathers grave, aren't saying much at all. All they know is that it was a Dragon, and it comes to Riley saying "Don't Fail Us." Of course, there's the always annoying collection agents who won't leave Riley alone even though being a minor absolves her from any of her parents debts.<br /><br />This is the big reveal in the end. When Oliver finally uncovers the reason why Paul was reincarnated, you know that Riley is the reason for it. Naturally, the whole good vs evil is once again in play. Who are the one's actually protecting the demon trappers Angels or Demons and why? Is Lucifer actually the bad guy, or the one who is there to stop the forthcoming Apocalypse from happening. Interesting in that Oliver really portrays Lucifer to be a decent enough character in that he is actually doing God's work in testing humans and angels alike and judging the worthy from the not.<br /><br />Ori, the so called Freelance demon hunter, is out for something other than protecting Riley from the Level 5 Demon who killed her father. Ori's revelation of who he is, and what he wants from Riley comes with a huge twist once again, in the end. I appreciate the fact that Oliver waited until the last chapters to reveal the underlying plots for Ori and Lucifer. Naturally, this is Riley's biggest mistake since she loses apart of herself that she can never get back.<br /><br />Demon Hunters sanctioned by the Vatican and requested by those in charge of Atlanta, arrive and aim directly for Riley. They believe that Paul and Riley are the main reasons why 1/3 of the cities demon trappers were killed by a massive demon attack on their meeting place. They pretty much just push the cities demon hunters to the side, and abruptly start killing every demon in sight. Of course, thanks to Simon ::coughasshatcough:: The demon hunters have Riley in their sights and are relentless in their pursuit.<br /><br />Then there's Simon who Riley agreed to work for Heaven if the angels would just save his life. Simon who Riley fell deeply in love with only to have her heart tore out of her body and stomped on. So much for gratitude! Simon turns out to be the worse sort of asshat I've had the displeasure to read about in a very long time. He is the worse sort of bible thumper as well and really puts Riley in a bind when he believes she has sold her soul to Lucifer.<br /><br />Riley and her best friend Peter have discovered that someone is definitely messing with the Holy Water in the city and diluting it with water. Unfortunately, with everything else that happens to Riley in this story, this becomes a tertiary storyline. Thankfully, Peter seems to be Riley's only real friend who doesn't go out of his way to betray her. Instead, he honestly does his best to help her get to the bottom of the holy water controversy.<br /><br />Beck. Ah, who can forget Beck? Beck is a journeyman demon trapper who worked for Riley's father and now considers himself to be her protector as well as her guardian. He is also an army veteran and loves to drink hard and listen to ::gasp:: country music! Beck is 5 years older than Riley and has always thought of her as his little sister. In this book, you get a sense that Beck actually cares for Riley, but the two of them are so hard headed that you wonder who they have co-existed so long without coming to blows. I really am disappointed in Beck however, when he falls into Justine Armando's clutches. Beck, Beck, Beck, Dude!!! <br /><br />Knowing this was the second novel in a 4 part series, I was a little tepid to read it. Normally the second book in a series is the best one of the bunch. This book, unfortunately, leaves readers with a HUGE cliffhanger and a reunion that I really ought to have seen coming.<br /><br />I love the world building for this series. The story takes place in a not too future Atlanta (2018) where the city is totally broke and the prices of everything is out of this world. It's a city that has turned into a battle ground between good and evil and those that fight the good fight.<br /><br />I do appreciate how Oliver hasn't turned Riley into a teetotaler or a coffee drinker. As a hot chocolate lover myself, I can totally respect a fellow chocolate lover. I just wish that Riley wouldn't come across as such a idiot most of the time. Overall, her choices from agreeing to work with Heaven to her new agreement with Lucifer, have all come with steep prices. <br /><br />You know when an author has grabbed your attention when you start screaming at the characters in the book like they were sitting right next to you. Oliver really puts her characters through the ringers, and I can only hope that the next book is as good as this one.<br /><br />Next in series:<br />Forgiven March 27, 2012<br />Foretold August 2, 2012<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16995320266099880533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_198159538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198159538" />
    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5019740-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311367304p2/5019740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198159538?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/5019740-alicia">Alicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198159538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer962709184468497659">**SPOILERS FOR FORSAKEN, THE FIRST BOOK IN THE SERIES (which you should definitely read first!)**<br/><br/>It’s a bit difficult to give a brief summary of Forbidden without revealing too much, as there are a heck of a lot of amazing plot twists which I really don’t want to spoil, but I’ll try my best: Forbidden starts where Forsaken left us – with the entire city of Atlanta recovering from the demon attack that occurred at the Demon Trapper meeting; Trappers are mourning the loss of some of their greatest</span>
  <span id="freeText962709184468497659" style="display:none">**SPOILERS FOR FORSAKEN, THE FIRST BOOK IN THE SERIES (which you should definitely read first!)**<br /><br />It’s a bit difficult to give a brief summary of Forbidden without revealing too much, as there are a heck of a lot of amazing plot twists which I really don’t want to spoil, but I’ll try my best: Forbidden starts where Forsaken left us – with the entire city of Atlanta recovering from the demon attack that occurred at the Demon Trapper meeting; Trappers are mourning the loss of some of their greatest as well as attempting to work out how they were attacked in the first place and the citizens of Atlanta are worried that they’re not being protected efficiently enough from the demons, which leads to the ruthlessly efficient Demon Hunters being called in – something the Trappers aren’t best pleased about. Meanwhile, Riley’s relationship with Simon is most definitely on the rocks, which leads to a growing attraction to the mysterious Ori, who vows to protect her from the deadly demon that is determined to kill her. Aside from all of this, she’s trying to figure out who brought her dad back from the dead and why someone is selling counterfeit Holy Water, as well as trying to earn enough to pay the rent.<br /><br />In case you haven’t read Forsaken and are completely confused, the series is set in an alternate world where demons roam freely, and are graded from very harmless (Grade One a.k.a. klepto-fiends) to extremely dangerous (Grade Five a.k.a. Geo-Fiends). Trappers and Hunters do as they say on the tin with regards to the getting rid of the demonic presences, and there’s quite a bit of a rivalry between the two. Witches and Necromancers (people who reanimate the dead to sell as slaves) also exist and trade freely in this alternate future of 2018. The series is set in Atlanta, which is desperately poor, and doing anything it can to save or increase money, including closing schools and housing classes in abandoned buildings or coffee shops. Riley is a Demon Trapper – one of the youngest, and the only female – whose father was recently killed by a demon, who is now after her.<br /><br />The events of Forsaken were recapped very well without seeming patronising or spelling things out as obviously as possible (which many books annoyingly do), and are much needed as I, for one, had forgotten several things having read the first book of this amazing series over six months ago. I can’t describe why I like Oliver’s writing and characterisation so much – you’ll just have to grab a copy yourself to see how captivating, insightful and creative it truly is! I also love the subtle but extremely funny humour laced throughout this brilliant book as it makes Forbidden an even more enjoyable read. It is, much like its predecessor, very creative – I especially liked the creepy reanimated-body auction and the idea of parking spaces as mini shops. I also adored the klepto-fiends–micro-sized demons with a penance for shiny things–along with Mort, the necromancer, who is such a nice and kind person, despite his job of bringing back the dead to work as slaves, but we get a very good insight into his back-story, which makes you extremely sympathetic towards him.<br /><br /> I’ve come to love Riley so much – she’s likeable, funny and down-to-earth, as well as being a really strong character, especially now she’s orphaned. Every single character in Forbidden is utterly unique, the vast majority realistic and most are surprisingly complex. The cover is stunningly striking, and I love the gorgeous blue flames that perfectly match the eyes of ‘Riley’ (and how drastically pale she has become), along with the fact that the style of Forsaken has been kept – it’ll be a lovely series to collect.<br /><br />However, I really didn’t like Simon, Riley’s saintly boyfriend who is barely recovering from the tragic demon attack at the Tabernacle, especially when he gets snappy with Riley, and I’m surprised that she still wanted to be with him for some time. I’m not sure if I like the accents showing up in the character’s (namely Beck and his Southern drawl and Stewart’s Scottish tongue) speech, though it does make for more realistic, if annoying, reading. Also, I was a bit confused by the whole Holy Water scam and didn’t properly understand how it worked, but it was probably just me. I was so glad to get an explanation as to how demons infiltrated earth, which was my only complaint about the first book, and the explanation was very surprising and revealing.<br /><br /> Forbidden is full of suspense as to who stole Riley’s father’s body, how the demons managed to break in at the Trapper Meeting and what exactly Ori is up to; combine that with brilliant writing and fantastic characters and you have yourself a real page-turner of a spectacular novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="962709184468497659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_625606814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625606814" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13213279-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370787077p2/13213279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/625606814?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/13213279-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13213279-siobhan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13213279-siobhan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13213279-siobhan?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer625606814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1050167895799894333">The Demon Trappers: Forbidden is the second book in Jana Oliver's series. It continues the story of seventeen year old Riley Blackthorne, the only female trapper in the Atlanta guild if Demon Trappers. Her father has been lifted from his grave and as the trappers try to come to terms with the death of so many trappers in the tabernacle debacle it creates more and more times for this poor girl to be taken advantage of and manipulated.<br/><br/>Ugh ugh guh RILEY!<br/><br/>Riley, baby, why?!<br/><br/>I finished this book last n</span>
  <span id="freeText1050167895799894333" style="display:none">The Demon Trappers: Forbidden is the second book in Jana Oliver's series. It continues the story of seventeen year old Riley Blackthorne, the only female trapper in the Atlanta guild if Demon Trappers. Her father has been lifted from his grave and as the trappers try to come to terms with the death of so many trappers in the tabernacle debacle it creates more and more times for this poor girl to be taken advantage of and manipulated.<br /><br />Ugh ugh guh RILEY!<br /><br />Riley, baby, why?!<br /><br />I finished this book last night and I just... in the last sixty pages I was gagging and voicing my frustration because Riley is just so broken and in need of help. I felt like shaking her and slapping some sense into her. She's a little girl, she's seventeen and she is an orphan for godsakes. I think she's allowed to be a bit reckless and stupid. She can't help it. It happens to be how she copes. It's just unfortunate that it gets her into so much trouble.<br /><br />Now, Riley isn't the only one who's is having a crap time. I was right to mistrust Simon. <s>Simon is nuttier than squirrel poo.</s> I feel bad that I was proven right on that because he was so nice in the first one, but he just always felt off to me.<br /><br />No one ever mention the name Ori within my presence unless we happen to be talking about the dwarf. Okay? That is all I have to say about this particular character. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Goddamn piece of Fallen Angel scum. I hated you and knew what you were from the first moment you walked into Riley's life, you piece of shit. I hope you're suffering in whatever circle of Hell Lucifer happened to drop you in. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There was a lot of character growth for Harper, Riley Master, and Mortimer, a kind necromancer. I just kept feeling like Riley needed a strong female presence in her life. I know she has Ayden (which honestly confuses me because there are so many beautiful Irish girls name and you name her after a boy... to each their own) and Simi, but neither of them have any real power or influence over her life and she really needs someone to help her. She is surrounded by men, and because of that she has become judgemental of women. I mean, I didn't like Justine either, but she could have not "hated" her because she was professionally dressed. That's in her job description.<br /><br />Beck. DENVER BECK I SWEAR TO HELL - If you've read the first book then you know that Denver is not the sharpest tool in the shed. He's an angry, damaged dude who had a lot of issues growing up. There's one particular scene that heart my heart. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is a spoiler that's not really a spoiler, the fact that Den can't read. That hit me hard because so many people cannot read and it's such an embarrassing and painful problem to have. So much stigma. Props to Den for being able to tell Riley because that would have to be one of the worst things he would ever have to say to anyone about himself, save the last minute confession about wanting to be in a relationship with her, but we'll leave that were it is. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, he should probably stay away from red heads, if you catch my drift.<br /><br />I feel like, as I finished the book, that I had gotten every person in this book marked down by the end of the first chapter. This isn't a bad thing, I happen to tack people and their written personalities down quickly. I saw the majority of this happening while I was reading the first book. Anyway, it was a good second book and I enjoyed it greatly. It wasn't as good as the first book for me, but I just got sick of Riley doubting Denver and everyone else and trusting people who would ultimately hurt her. Well, that's her choice and I respect that, but, baby, please.<br /><br />I enjoyed the book, same kind of pacing as the first and it was fun to read. I will be continuing onto the next book.<br />Happy reading.<br /><br />Chaos out.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_171162650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171162650" />
    <a title="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5386619-nina-s"><img alt="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433066789p2/5386619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171162650?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" href="/user/show/5386619-nina-s">Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=utopian-dystopian">utopian-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171162650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12171771051841523124"><i>"Riley's beginning to think being a demon trapper isn't all it's cracked up to be. Her dad's been stolen by a necromancer, her boyfriend's gone all weird and she's getting warm and fuzzy feelings for someone who's seriously bad news. It's tempting to give it all up and try to be normal, but that's not an option. Because the demons have plans for Riley. And they're not the only ones."</i> <--That is the synopsis on the back of the book. It pretty much does sum up the entire story!<br/><br/><b>Forbidden</b> is definit</span>
  <span id="freeText12171771051841523124" style="display:none"><i>"Riley's beginning to think being a demon trapper isn't all it's cracked up to be. Her dad's been stolen by a necromancer, her boyfriend's gone all weird and she's getting warm and fuzzy feelings for someone who's seriously bad news. It's tempting to give it all up and try to be normal, but that's not an option. Because the demons have plans for Riley. And they're not the only ones."</i> &lt;--That is the synopsis on the back of the book. It pretty much does sum up the entire story!<br /><br /><b>Forbidden</b> is definitely unexpected, and when I say unexpected, it did the things I didn't want it to. Since I loved the first one so much I wanted to love this one just as much too. <br /><br /><b>WHAT I DIDN'T LIKE</b><br /><b>1.</b> ORI. I didn't like Ori, he was the perfect dark and mysterious stranger. And then he turned into what he did! I hate that the last scene we see of him before <i>what happens</i>. It was completely not smooth.<br /><b>2.</b> RILEY. She was kinda kick ass in the first one, but in this one she's not! It was so irritating that she became so obsessed with guys when there were so many other important things to worry about.<br /><b>3.</b> The multiple lovers Riley seems to have. She gets around quick, Simon then Ori then... and the worse part is that Jana Oliver really plays on Riley's youth and naivety. One moment Riley is old enough and strong enough to trap demons. The next she's making the worst, most irrational decisions ever!<br /><br /><b>WHAT I DID LIKE</b><br /><b>1.</b> THE LORE. I love the mythology that Oliver created behind the history of Trappers and Hunters and Demons. IT is completely confusing but thought out. I like this new look to Angels and Demons, God and Lucifer.<br /><b>2.</b> The tension. The tension between Beck and Riley is still there. To be honest normally I find overly romantic novels a pain in the ass to read, but this time the tension is so hot, it makes me want to read more just to see if they do ever get together. <br /><b>3.</b> The story. I like the story that happens in the background of Riley's love life, I just wish it stood out more. It's absolutely fascinating, the images Oliver creates in my mind of this dystopia.<br /><b>4.</b> The repeated image of the warriors. I really liked the image that Oliver described. The ring of glowing angels that surrounded the Tabernacle. It was amazing. I could totally draw it! ~if only I was a better drawer.<br /><br />Overall, Jana Oliver doesn't disappoint, even if it took a while to get past the Riley's love life to the story underneath. If you aren't aren't a reader of romantic escapades of any kind then you probably won't like this one even though the story is mainly is about Riley. If you love supernatural fiction this is for you. It's definitely not disappointing in that aspect, which is why it earned 3 stars from me. It lost two because it took so long for me to get into the story. But once it started rolling, the pages wouldn't stop turning... ;P </span>

<div id="review_190322432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190322432" />
    <a title="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4561998-carmel-rabid-reads"><img alt="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396922701p2/4561998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190322432?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmel (Rabid Reads)" href="/user/show/4561998-carmel-rabid-reads">Carmel (Rabid Reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312614799" href="/book/show/10368915-soul-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190322432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3170392383259155205"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://www.rabidreads.com/2011/11/review-soul-thief-by-jana-oliver.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>I adored the fast paced, distinctive storyline of <i>The Demon Trapper's Daughter</i> which made <i>Soul Thief</i> an automatic add to my must-read pile. Jana Oliver's second installment is good but the change in the plot's direction does have me concerned. I was really hoping for some romance this time around, instead we get something else entirely and I'm still not sure how I feel about it. Beck, Simon and Ori all had the potential of being sexy alpha males except they act like compl</span>
  <span id="freeText3170392383259155205" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://www.rabidreads.com/2011/11/review-soul-thief-by-jana-oliver.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>I adored the fast paced, distinctive storyline of <i>The Demon Trapper's Daughter</i> which made <i>Soul Thief</i> an automatic add to my must-read pile. Jana Oliver's second installment is good but the change in the plot's direction does have me concerned. I was really hoping for some romance this time around, instead we get something else entirely and I'm still not sure how I feel about it. Beck, Simon and Ori all had the potential of being sexy alpha males except they act like complete morons 99% of the time. <i>Soul Thief</i> delivers a very different feel than its predecessor and I'm not sure if I like it.<br><br>Things have gone from bad to worse since we last saw Riley. This poor girl just can't get a break! The demons know her name, her dad's now among the walking dead, her (ex) boyfriend is convinced that she made a deal with the Devil, and the list continues! There aren't even any little victories; no glimpses of hope. As a result, the story felt very weight downed with little to look forward to anytime soon. I understand that life is different here. Future Atlanta is not a pretty place but still, small victories, right? Life has to give us a few good moments here and there otherwise what's the point!?<br><br>I was really hopping that Beck would make a move on Riley but alas he only morphs into an even bigger stick in the mudd. No one can be that good intentioned! C'mon people, it's the end of the world! Do you really want to spend it alone? Okay, so her guardian's a no-go but what about Simon and Ori? I'm afraid that there's not much to report on either front. Simon is now the biggest douche in Oliver's universe and as for Ori... eeeck! Completely unexpected! I'm also a little angered by what Jana does to his character. He was the light at the end of the tunnel. Probably not Riley's forever but at least they could have cheered each other up for a while. Not anymore! <br><br>It wasn't all bad though. I enjoyed the parts where miss Blackthorne and her BFF team up to investigate the holy water problem. He's a nice distraction and Riley seems to act more like herself whenever Peter's around. One especially cute moment stands out to me when they use technology to trap a Klepto-Fiend. Go teamwork! <br><br>The ending left me on the fence as to whether I want to give <i>Forgiven</i> a try. It'll all depend on how Oliver decides to play her hand. <i>Soul Thief</i> was just a passable read compared to book 1 but maybe it was a necessary bump in the road and the follow-up will make everything better. It's hard to say, but after such a strong start to this series with <i>The Demon Trapper's Daughter</i>, I'm willing to keep an open mind.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379760608i/196069.png" height="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3170392383259155205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_162131347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162131347" />
    <a title="Μαρία Γεωργοπούλου" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4903642"><img alt="Μαρία Γεωργοπούλου" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522132931p2/4903642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162131347?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Μαρία Γεωργοπούλου" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Μαρία Γεωργοπούλου" href="/user/show/4903642">Μαρία Γεωργοπούλου</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162131347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8873236656252806749">OMG! This book was AMAZING! “Forbidden” is the second book in the Demon Trappers series by Jana Oliver and I have to say that it was even better than the first one! I don’t really know from where to start this review! This world-building is the most interesting in a YA fantasy book. While I was reading the story I thought that I was a part of this world. Although there is enough misery and the whole atmosphere is very dark, the writing style of the author is so good that I wanted to live there a</span>
  <span id="freeText8873236656252806749" style="display:none">OMG! This book was AMAZING! “Forbidden” is the second book in the Demon Trappers series by Jana Oliver and I have to say that it was even better than the first one! I don’t really know from where to start this review! This world-building is the most interesting in a YA fantasy book. While I was reading the story I thought that I was a part of this world. Although there is enough misery and the whole atmosphere is very dark, the writing style of the author is so good that I wanted to live there and be a demon trapper myself!<br /><br />I have to admit that this book is a “difficult” one. What I mean with this? Well, except from the adventure and the cool moments there are some very difficult decisions to be made by the main characters. Also, there is a lot of pain, betrayal, loss and some very-very-very bad decisions. You think you know some of the characters but then come times that you understand that you will be very surprised by them. <br /><br />The story starts where the fist book stops. Riley has too many problems: Her dad is dead and his body has been stolen. Simon, her boyfriend isn’t the same anymore. Beck is a pain for her, as always and, Ori, is pretty hot but with too many secrets. She doesn’t know who to trust and that’s why all hell breaks loose… literally! <br /><br />Riles is an amazing girl but she has a lot in her plate. Yes, she made some bad decisions. Yes, she should be more careful and not so trustful. But, give her a break! She is a seventeen year old girl without family and with many financial problems. She is the only girl in a very difficult job and she doesn’t have time to relax at all. Everybody treats her as a little girl sometimes and other times as an adult. It’s confusing!<br /><br />But let’s talk about the male characters now. Simon first. I really don’t want to talk about him. He was such a good guy in the first book but now he is a jerk. I don’t think that he has an excuse. It’s easy to blame the most weak person and he’s doing it! Not good at all. <br /><br />Ori isn’t what I was expecting. At all. I don’t want to write any spoilers but I have to say that his behavior through the whole book was kind of strange and I had the feeling that something wasn’t right. Yes, he is sexy but that doesn’t mean that he is good!<br /><br />It’s known from my review for the first book that I am team Beck all the way! And after I read this book, I am still at the same team. But the truth to be told, in this story nothing goes well with him also. I still have hope and I want to see him happy because he is such a great guy! Strong and brave, Beck is the kind of man who will protect his woman no matter what.<br /><br />I love this series so far! The story is very well-written and kept my interest from the first page until the last. Of course, I’ll start reading the next book from this series right away! Thank you Jana Oliver for another amazing book!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8873236656252806749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E073HfN9mJO+6axUAZK4XrLHnx+yettwRokUQMlMhA3872GEeyVHbeDeBjpKlkM2/SPohvfagYhquoyE0IOGFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6Q9JoRG/jWYxtRfMpB7e5NeqvJE9IgpVNbSvNArqSN0Grt84medSmG+CvaLvGiWMmE7LCHiCUK0ZhzfwEyVKxQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer7304332514638284050">Jana Oliver is an international and Amazon bestselling author who lives in Portugal.<br/><br/>Her novels have won numerous awards, including the Prism Award, the Daphne du Maurier Award for Excellence in Mystery and Supense as well as the National Readers' Choice Award. <br/><br/>Her books include The Demon Trappers Series and Briar Rose (Young Adult), time travel/historical mystery (The Time Rovers Series) and paran</span>
  <span id="freeText7304332514638284050" style="display:none">Jana Oliver is an international and Amazon bestselling author who lives in Portugal.<br /><br />Her novels have won numerous awards, including the Prism Award, the Daphne du Maurier Award for Excellence in Mystery and Supense as well as the National Readers' Choice Award. <br /><br />Her books include The Demon Trappers Series and Briar Rose (Young Adult), time travel/historical mystery (The Time Rovers Series) and paranormal romance (Tangled Souls).<br /><br />She is co-author of Socially Engaged: The Author's Guide to Social media, written with Tyra Burton.<br /><br />She is happiest when she's researching urban legends, peering at old maps and adding to her growing collection of port and Portuguese wines. <br /><br /><br /></span>
